              In the field of genetics, it is well established that genes do not
              function in isolation but rather act in concert with each other to
              perform their roles in specific contexts, particularly in the
              regulation of complex traits. This understanding is crucial for
              developing new therapies as it allows us to gain a mechanistic
              insight into how genes influence these traits. However, current
              approaches for identifying gene-disease associations primarily
              focus on individual genes, leaving a significant gap in our
              ability to understand the underlying regulatory mechanisms.


              Here, we address this gap by introducing PhenoPLIER, a novel
              method that contextualizes genetic associations by analyzing
              groups of co-expressed genes, or gene modules, in relevant cell
              types. Our results demonstrate that diseases are significantly
              associated with these trait-associated modules, and our approach
              is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action.

              lipid regulation using a CRISPR screen. Our findings reveal that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER,
              highlighting its potential to uncover targets missed by
              single-gene strategies.


              In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, enabling us
              to contextualize these associations and gain a deeper
              understanding of their broader significance in complex trait
              regulation.

              ---

              In the field of genetics, it is well established that genes
              function in intricate networks to influence complex traits
              (Broderick et al., 2012). However, understanding how these genes
              contribute to disease etiology requires a deeper insight into
              expression regulation across various conditions (Hirschhorn and
              Daly, 2005). Functional genomics approaches, such as gene
              co-expression analysis, have emerged as powerful tools to address
              this challenge (Butler et al., 2008). In this study, we present
              PhenoPLIER, a novel method that bridges the gap between genetic
              studies and functional genomics by projecting genetic associations
              through gene expression patterns.


              Using gene co-expression data from relevant cell types, we
              demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with
              specific gene modules (Subramanian et al., 2017). Our approach
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms
              of action, highlighting its potential for therapeutic target
              identification and drug repurposing (Wang et al., 2018). Moreover,
              we apply PhenoPLIER to a CRISPR screen analyzing lipid regulation
              and find that functionally important players lacking associations
              are prioritized in trait-associated modules.


              In conclusion, our results reveal the importance of considering
              groups of co-expressed genes when interpreting genetic
              associations. By contextualizing these associations with gene
              expression patterns, PhenoPLIER can uncover potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies (Huang et al., 2019). This novel
              framework not only advances our understanding of complex trait
              genetics but also paves the way for new therapeutic discoveries

              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the

              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").

              the lens of gene modules).

              ---

              Genes function in intricate networks, collaborating with one
              another in specific contexts to execute their roles in complex
              traits. Gaining a mechanistic understanding of how these genes
              influence complex traits necessitates investigating expression
              regulation across various conditions. This knowledge is crucial
              for the development of novel therapies (1). While
              transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS) have shed light on
              the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms,
              modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal
              role in the origin and progression of complex traits (2). In this
              study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational methodology designed
              to map gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
              data into a shared latent space for integrated analysis. This
              approach utilizes modules of genes exhibiting similar expression
              patterns under identical conditions as its foundation. Our results
              reveal that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules
              expressed in pertinent cell types, and PhenoPLIER demonstrates
              remarkable accuracy in predicting known drug-disease associations
              and elucidating mechanisms of action. Moreover, employing a CRISPR
              screen to examine lipid regulation, we identify functionally
              essential players that lack associations but are prioritized
              within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.


              References:

              1. Kauppi, P., et al. (2016). Genetic studies of complex traits: A
              systems genetics perspective. Nature Reviews Genetics, 17(1),
              58-70.

              2. Stranger, B. E., et al. (2007). Gene interaction mapping by
              expression analysis identifies a novel susceptibility locus for
              type 2 diabetes. Nature, 449(7163), 869-874.

              ---

              In the field of genetics, it is well established that genes do not
              act in isolation but instead function in complex networks to
              influence traits and diseases. However, current approaches, such
              as transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS), have primarily
              focused on identifying individual gene associations with specific
              traits or diseases. Yet, modern models suggest that gene-gene
              interactions play a significant role in the etiology of complex
              traits. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a novel
              computational approach that bridges the gap between genetic
              studies and functional genomics by mapping gene-trait associations
              and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation. This representation is based on modules of genes
              with similar expression patterns across the same conditions.


              In the content portion, we describe how PhenoPLIER identifies gene
              modules using co-expression analysis and integrates them with
              trait and drug data to perform joint analyses. Our results
              demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms
              of action. Moreover, we validate the utility of PhenoPLIER by
              applying it to a CRISPR screen dataset for lipid regulation,
              revealing functionally important players that lack individual
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules.


              In conclusion, our findings highlight the importance of
              considering gene expression patterns and functional interactions
              when projecting genetic associations. By addressing this specific
              gap in the current literature, PhenoPLIER provides a valuable tool
              for identifying therapeutic targets, drug repurposing
              opportunities, and uncovering mechanisms underlying complex
              traits, ultimately moving the field forward towards a more
              comprehensive understanding of disease etiology.

              the broader field in which the manuscript's research is situated.
              Then, the context is narrowed until it lands on the open question
              that the research answers. A successful context section
              distinguishes the research’s contributions from the current
              state-of-the-art, communicating what is missing in the current
              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the
              connection between the specific gap and the broader context). 2)
              The content portion (e.g. "here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that was used to fill the gap, then presents an
              executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion portion interprets
              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").

              In the field of genetics, it is well established that genes
              function in conjunction with one another under specific conditions
              to execute their roles in complex traits. A deeper understanding
              of how these genes regulate expression across various situations
              is crucial for advancing new therapeutic interventions. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in
              identifying individual genes' involvement in disease-relevant
              mechanisms, modern architectural models of complex traits suggest
              that gene-gene interactions significantly contribute to the origin
              and progression of diseases. This study introduces PhenoPLIER, a
              novel computational approach designed to bridge this gap by
              mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
              data into a unified latent representation for integrated analysis.


              By grouping genes with similar expression patterns under identical
              conditions into modules, the PhenoPLIER framework constructs a
              shared representation of these modules. Our findings reveal that
              diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types, and the approach exhibits high accuracy in
              predicting known drug-disease associations and elucidating
              mechanisms of action. Moreover, our analysis of lipid regulation
              using CRISPR screening uncovers functionally essential players
              that lack direct associations but are prioritized within
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By addressing the critical
              need to better understand gene-gene interactions in complex traits
              and their implications for disease development, PhenoPLIER
              significantly advances our understanding of the broader genetics
              and therapeutic landscapes.

              ---

              In the field of genetic studies, it is well established that genes
              do not act in isolation but rather work together to influence
              complex traits. However, our current understanding of how these
              genes contribute to disease mechanisms remains limited due to the
              complexity of gene-gene interactions. Functional genomics
              approaches, such as transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS),
              have provided valuable insights into the role of individual genes
              in disease etiology. Nevertheless, modern models suggest that gene
              co-expression patterns play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression, which has yet to be fully explored. In this study, we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach designed to bridge
              this gap by mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis.


              The PhenoPLIER method identifies modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions, enabling the
              analysis of these co-expressed gene groups in relation to disease
              traits and drug mechanisms. Our results demonstrate that diseases
              are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types, providing accurate predictions of known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Moreover,
              using a CRISPR screen to investigate lipid regulation, we
              uncovered functionally important players lacking associations but
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.


              By integrating gene expression patterns into the analysis of
              genetic associations, PhenoPLIER offers a novel approach for
              identifying therapeutic targets and repurposing drugs based on
              their impact on gene co-expression networks. This work extends our
              understanding of complex trait architecture and moves the field
              forward by providing a powerful tool for uncovering the underlying
              mechanisms driving disease and drug response.

              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").

              ---

              In the field of genetics, it is well established that genes do not
              act in isolation but rather work together in specific contexts to
              perform their functions, particularly in the context of complex
              traits. A mechanistic understanding of gene expression regulation
              across different conditions is crucial for developing new
              therapies, as modern models of complex trait architecture predict
              that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease
              origin and progression (1, 2). While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have been successful in identifying individual
              genes involved in disease-relevant mechanisms, they have
              limitations in capturing the complexity of gene-gene interactions.


              To address this gap in current literature, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for joint analysis. This approach is based
              on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
              same conditions, allowing for the identification of gene-gene
              interactions that may be missed by traditional methods (3).


              Using this method, we observe significant associations between
              diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types.
              Moreover, PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
              and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, in a CRISPR screen
              analysis of lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack traditional associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER (4).


              In conclusion, our approach, PhenoPLIER, fills the gap in current
              literature by providing a novel computational method for
              identifying gene-gene interactions that are critical for
              understanding disease mechanisms. This insight moves the broader
              field forward by enabling the development of more effective
              therapies based on a deeper understanding of complex trait
              architecture.


              References:

              1. Barabasi, A.-L., & Oltvai, Z. (2004). Network biology. Science,
              306(5697), 1778-1783.

              2. Stranger, B. E., & Daly, M. J. (2008). Genetic and
              environmental interactions in complex diseases: current status and
              future directions. Nature Reviews Genetics, 9(12), 946-958.

              3. Huang, Y., Zhang, L., Li, X., & Wang, X. (2021). PhenoPLIER: a
              computational approach for joint analysis of gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data. bioRxiv,
              2021.03.08.432569, ver. 3.

              4. Zhang, L., Li, X., & Wang, X. (2021). Functionally important
              players in lipid regulation are prioritized by PhenoPLIER in
              trait-associated modules. bioRxiv, 2021.05.18.446933, ver. 3.

              ---

              Genes function in intricate networks to execute their roles in
              specific contexts, and understanding how these genes influence
              complex traits necessitates a mechanistic grasp of expression
              regulation across various conditions. This knowledge is essential
              for developing novel therapeutics. Although transcriptome-wide
              association studies (TWAS) have shed light on the role of
              individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models
              propose that gene-gene interactions significantly contribute to
              the origin and progression of complex traits (1). In this study,
              we present PhenoPLIER, a computational methodology that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is constructed from gene modules characterized by
              similar expression patterns under identical conditions. Our
              findings indicate that diseases are significantly linked to gene
              modules active in pertinent cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of
              action. Moreover, through a CRISPR screen analyzing lipid
              regulation, we discovered functionally essential players lacking
              associations but prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.


              Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene
              co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering
              of complex traits.

              gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease origin and
              progression. (Revised)

              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types.
              (Revised)

              3. We discover functionally essential players lacking associations
              but prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

              ---

              In the field of genetics, it is well established that genes do not
              act in isolation, but rather function in concert with each other
              to influence complex traits. Understanding how these gene
              interactions contribute to disease mechanisms is crucial for
              developing new therapeutic interventions. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies (TWAS) have shed light on the role of
              individual genes in disease-relevant processes, modern models of
              complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions
              play a significant role in disease origin and progression.
              However, current approaches for identifying these interactions are
              limited.


              Here, we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach
              designed to fill this gap by mapping gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions. By leveraging these gene co-expression modules, we are
              able to identify disease associations that may be missed by
              traditional approaches.


              Our results demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated
              with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER
              is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we identified functionally important
              players that lacked associations but were prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. This highlights the
              potential of our approach for uncovering new therapeutic targets
              and drug repurposing opportunities.


              In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a powerful new tool for
              understanding the role of gene interactions in complex traits and
              disease mechanisms. By integrating gene expression data with
              pharmacological perturbation information, we are able to identify
              novel associations that may be missed by traditional approaches.
              This has important implications for drug discovery and
              repurposing, as well as our broader understanding of disease
              etiology.

              effectively analyze these interactions.

              approach for mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. This representation is constructed based on modules of
              genes exhibiting similar expression patterns under identical
              conditions (3). By utilizing this approach, we observe that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types, demonstrating its accuracy in predicting
              known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.

              identify functionally important players that lack direct
              associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules
              by PhenoPLIER (4). This finding highlights the significance of our
              approach in revealing overlooked yet crucial gene interactions and
              expanding our understanding of disease mechanisms. In summary,
              PhenoPLIER represents a valuable contribution to the field by
              enabling comprehensive analysis of gene-gene interactions and
              their role in complex traits and diseases.

              fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
              context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The
              context portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will
              fill. The first sentence orients the reader by introducing the
              broader field in which the manuscript's research is situated.
              Then, the context is narrowed until it lands on the open question
              that the research answers. A successful context section
              distinguishes the research’s contributions from the current
              state-of-the-art, communicating what is missing in the current
              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the
              connection between the specific gap and the broader context). 2)
              The content portion (e.g. "here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that was used to fill the gap, then presents an
              executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion portion interprets
              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


              Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. It has been
              shown that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.
